Officcs—1G, Marshall Street. 13 REPORT OF THE VESTRY of the Parish of St. James, Westminster, FOR THE YEAR 1893-94. Vestry Hall, Piccadilly, W., April, 1894. In accordance with the provisions of the Metropolis Local Management Act, 1855, the Vestry present the following Report of their proceedings and an abstract of their accounts for the twelve months ended the 25th March last; also a statement of Contracts entered into or in force during that time, and the liabilities of the Vestry at the end thereof, together with the Report of their Surveyor for the same period, and of their Medical Officer of Health for the year 1893. With a view to affording the ratepayers as complete a knowledge as possible of the administration of parochial affairs generally, the Vestry again append to their Report, Statements of Accounts relating to the Guardians of the Westminster Union, the Commissioners for Public Baths and Wash-houses, and the Trustees of Charitable Endowments in which the parish is interested, 14 THE PARISH. Extent.—The Parish occupies an area of 162 acres. It has about 12½ miles of streets, of which 3½ miles are paved with wood, 5¼ with asphalte, ¾ with pitching, 1½ with macadam, and 1½ miles consists of courts, yards, and passages. Population.—The resident population, according to the census taken on the 6th April, 1891, is given by the Registrar-General as 24,995, and the number of inhabited houses as 2,641. Local Government.—The Parish has a separate jurisdiction under the Metropolis Local Management Act, and particulars of the powers of the Vestry elected pursuant to that Act are given on page 18. For Poor Law purposes the Parish is joined to the Parish of St. Anne, under the name of the Westminster Union; it is also a constituent part of the Central London Sick Asylum District. Wards.—The Parish has been divided into four Wards for the election of Vestrymen, and this division is followed in the preparation of the Lists of Voters for Member of Parliament, the County Council, and School Board. The name of the Ward is printed on the rate receipt of each ratepayer. For Ecclesiastical Purposes the Parish has been subdivided into five districts, the mother church being St. James's, Piccadilly, of which the Rev. J. E. Kempe, M.A. is Rector. 15 Representation in Parliament.—The Parish of St. James was formerly comprised in the Parliamentary Borough of the City of Westminster, which returned two Members to Parliament; it now, however, forms a part of the Borough of Strand, which returns one member, the present representative being the Hon. W. F. D. Smith. The Register prepared in 1893 contains the names of 3,988 Parliamentary electors, viz., 2 on the Scot and Lot List, 280 Lodgers, and 3,706 possessing other qualifications. There are also 539 County Electors who have been placed on the Register under the Local Government Act, 1888, but are not qualified to vote for Members of Parliament. Parliamentary voters for the County of Middlesex, in respect of property situate wholly or in part in the Parish of St. James, number 180. By the Elementary Education Act, 1870, the Parish is included in the Westminster Division of the School Board for London, Five members of the School Board are elected by the ratepayers of the Division, the present members being Lord Colchester, General Sim, Mr. David Laing, Mr. William Winnett, and Mr. H. N. B. Spink. Water Supply.—Four Companies supply the Parish with water, the approximate boundaries of their respective districts being as follows :— 1. Chelsea Waterworks Company (Chief Office, 35, Commercial Road, Pimlico,). So much of the Parish as lies to the South of the centre of Pall Mall and Cleveland Row. This Company was incorporated by Royal Charter in the year 1722. 16 2. New River Company (Chief Office, Clerkenwell, E.C.). So much of the Parish as lies to the east of a line running at the back of the east side of Poland Street, Lexington Street, Great Windmill Street, and along the centre of the Haymarket. This Company was incorporated by Royal Charter in the year 1619. 3. Grand Junction Waterworks Company (Chief Office, 65, South Molton Street). So much of the Parish as lies to the West of the District supplied by the New River Company and the north of the centre of Pall Mall. This Company was incorporated by Act of Parliament in 1811. 4. West Middlesex Waterworks Company (Chief Office, 19, Marylebone Road). So much of Oxford Street as is situate within the Parish. This Company was incorporated by Act of Parliament in the year 1806. The rates of charge for a supply of water for domestic purposes authorised by the various Acts of Parliament relating to the several above-mentioned Companies are almost identical, the scale being as follows :— Where the annual value of the dwelling-house or other place does not exceed £200, a rate not exceeding 4 per cent. per annum; where such annual value exceeds £200, a rate not exceeding 3 per cent. per annum. An additional charge, varying from 4s. per annum where the annual value of the house exceeds £30, but is less than £50, to 12s. where the annual value of the house exceeds £300, is permitted for each single water-closet, fixed bath, or high service; for each additional water-closet, fixed bath, or high service 17 half these rates are to be charged. High service is defined as a delivery of water at an elevation of more than ten feet above the pavement in front of the dwelling-house or other place supplied. The Companies may supply water for other than domestic purposes, either upon agreed terms or by meter at a specified rate. Gas is supplied to the whole Parish by the Gas Light and Coke Company (Chief Office, Horseferry Road). Electricity, both for purposes of light and power, is supplied by the London Electric Supply Corporation and the St. James's and Pall Mall Electric Light Company. Each of these. Companies has parliamentary power to supply in any part of the Parish, and is under compulsion to supply any parishioner upon certain specified conditions. The former Company supply an alternating current, with the use of converters or transformers, the latter supply a direct continuous current. The offices of the London Company are at 3, Adelphi Terrace, W.C., and those of the St. James's Company at Carnaby Street. The Coroner is Mr. John Troutbeck, whose jurisdiction extends throughout the City and Liberties of Westminster. For the Registration of Births and Deaths the Parish is included in the Westminster District. The Sub- Registrar is Mr. Thomas Matthew Crowe, of 31, Wardour © Street; and the Superintendent Registrar, Mr. Joseph Bond, Union Offices, Poland Street. B 18 THE VESTRY, as now constituted under the Metropolis Local Management Act, 1855, consists of 48 elected and three ex-officio members, the latter being the Rector and Churchwardens. It superseded a Vestry elected under the provisions of a permissive statute, 1 & 2 William IV., cap. 60, which was adopted by the ratepayers of St. James's on the 6th April, 1832. This elected Vestry had, in its turn, superseded a select Vestry established by the Act under which the Parish was created in 1685. The select Vestry was virtually a self-appointed body, vacancies being filled up by the surviving members. Neither the ancient select Vestry nor the Vestry elected under the statute of 1831 had any jurisdiction over the paving or drainage of the Parish. Each of these matters was under the control of a separate and distinct body of Commissioners. The Act of 1855 transferred to the Vestry as now constituted, not only all the powers of the earlier Vestry, but also those relating to paving, drainage, and lighting formerly exercised by these Commissioners. Subsequent legislation has laid upon the Vestry various additional duties, and in many respects, the powers of the Vestry within the area of its jurisdiction resemble those of the Town Council of a corporate town, with the addition of rating powers, although as regards the police force, the provision of markets, and the supply of gas and water, not this Parish alone, but the metropolis at large, stands on a different footing from provincial towns of comparatively minor importance. The following pages will show the diversity of subjects coming within the purview of the Vestry, but it may be 19 convenient here to enumerate the more important functions of that body, viz.:— (1) Paving, cleansing, watering, and lighting the public streets. (2) Constructing, maintaining, and cleansing local sewers, public conveniences, etc. (3) Supervising the construction, alteration, and amendment of the drains and sanitary arrangements of dwelling-houses and other buildings. (4) Preventing, removing, and abating nuisances injurious to health, disinfecting after sickness &c. (5) Regulating projections into the public streets, and annoyances of various kinds. (6) Preserving, as far as possible, freedom from adulteration in articles of food and medicine. (7) Levying and collecting the rates, from which large and, unfortunately rapidly increasing, sums are paid annually to authorities entirely independent of local control. Upon the last-mentioned point it may be here observed that there has been a growing tendency for some years to include in the local rates various sums for Metropolitan purposes. Thus since the year 1855 the Vestry have at different times been required by Parliament to provide funds for—(a) Main Drainage; (b) Fire Brigade; (c) Elementary Education; (d) Thames Bridges—purchase maintenance, and re-building: (e) Artizans' Dwellings, and other purposes, The extent to which this operates upon b 2 20 local rates will be seen on reference to the statement of moneys raised with the parochial rates for Metropolitan purposes, which is given on page 38. THE ELECTION OF VESTRYMEN AND AUDITORS OF ACCOUNTS Was held on Monday, the 29th day of May, the places appointed for the purposes being—Pall Mall Ward, Willis's Restaurant, King Street, St. James's; Church Ward, Vestry Hall, Piccadilly; Golden Square Ward, Craven Hall, Marshall Street; and Great Marlborough Ward, Board Room, Poland Street. 9 The total expense of conducting the elections amounted to £7 16s. 6d., and an order for the payment of this sum from the Poor Rate was made by the vestry in accordance with the statute. RESIGNATIONS. During the year the following Vestrymen have resigned their seats:— Mr. C. E. Baxter Pall Mall Ward Mr. W. H. Dodwell The Vestry have to announce with regret the death of the following members during the year:— Mr. A. W. Dixey, (Church Ward), Mr. G. Biggs, (Church Ward), and Mr. R. Moore (Great Marlborough Ward.) Mr. Dixey had been a much respected member of the Vestry for many years, and for the past five years acted as Chairman of the Finance Committee. 21 Mr. Biggs, also another most respected member of the Vestry, had been a member since 1886, and after Mr. Dixey's death, was appointed Chairman of the Finance Committe, a position which he occupied until the time of his decease. Mr. Moore was appointed a member of the Vestry in 1801, but he did not take a very active part in the administration of the affairs of the Parish. A list of the Vestrymen and Auditors of Accounts will be found on pages 7 and 8. VESTRY AND COMMITTEE MEETINGS. The following is the number of meetings held during the year Vestry Meetings 25 Finance and House Committee 22 Sanitary, Parliamentary Bills, and General Purposes Committee 21 Works and Improvements Committee 21 Lighting Committee 8 St. James's Dwellings Committee 12 Valuation Committee 8 Special and Sub-Committees 9 Total 126 The Vestry usually meet on alternate Thursday mornings but a special meeting may be convened at any time upon the requisition of five members, and some of the ordinary meetings are suspended at vacation times. Five Standing Committees are appointed annually, in accordance with the 22 bye-laws of the Vestry, and meet as frequently as occasion may require. Special Committees are appointed from time to time to consider subjects not coming within the ordinary duties of either of the Standing Committees. OFFICERS OF THE VESTRY. Vestry Clerk.—The Vestry and the Parish have sustained a severe loss by the resignation of their able Vestry Clerk, Mr. Harry Wilkins, on his appointment to the Secretaryship of the Lambeth Waterworks Company. Mr. Wilkins was appointed to the office of Vestry Clerk in September, 1882, and has performed the duties devolving upon him with marked ability and. faithfulness. In addition to performing the ordinary duties of the office, Mr. Wilkins has from time to time identified himself with, and taken a prominent part in, various public and metropolitan questions, such as Electric Lighting, School Board Administration, London Water Supply, Assessment of Property, etc., and his loss to the Local Government of the Metropolis will be therefore more keenly felt. The Vestry, in accepting Mr. Wilkins' resignation, passed the following resolution, a copy of which was suitably engrossed on vellum and framed, and handed to Mr. Wilkins :— "That, in accepting with great reluctance the resignation of Mr. Harry Wilkins, their Vestry Clerk, the Vestry desire to place on record their testimony to the great ability, assiduity, and faithfulness Avith which for a period of nearly twelve years he has performed the duties pertaining to his office. His intimate knowledge of assessments and other matters relating to municipal life render his withdrawal from Vestry work a loss to London, a loss that at the present juncture it can ill afford." 23 Mr. Thomas Hensman Munsey, chief clerk to the Vestry of Islington, has been appointed Vestry Clerk in succession to Mr. Wilkins. Mr. Munsey was previously in the service of the Vestry, as First Assistant Clerk, from 1885 to 1889, in which latter year he left to take up the appointment at Islington. Vestry Clerk's Department.—The salary of Mr. Chettleburgh, first assistant clerk, has been increased from £150 to £180 per annum; that of Mr. Crow, accounts, rates, and general clerk, from £170 to £190; that of Mr. Lampard, third assistant clerk, from £100 to £120; and that of Mr. Born, junior clerk, from £20 to £30; all the increases to take effect from Lady Day, 1894. Sanitary Department,—The Vestry have found it necessary to engage a clerk to assist in the clerical work of the Sanitary and Surveyor's Departments, and they have accordingly appointed Mr. T. H. Hooper to the post, at a salary of £80 per annum. The salary of the public analyst, Dr. Edmunds, has been increased from £75 to £100 per annum; while that of the chief sanitary inspector, Mr. W. H. Watson, has been raised from £165 to £175 par annum, both these increases to take effect from the 25th March, 1894. In the early part of the year the salary of Mr. Folland, sanitary inspector, was increased from £120 to £140 per annum. Rate Collectors.—Mr. George Flint, of 18, Warwick, Street, has been appointed rate collector for the Pall Mall Ward, in the place of Mr. F. A. Ashmead, whose resignation was reported in the last annual report. 24 The Vestry handed to Mr. Ashmead a letter, under their common seal, expressing their regret that he felt compelled to relinquish his appointment, and their appreciation of his faithful and efficient services as collector of rates in the Pall Mall Ward for over seventeen years. Generally.—A list of the officers of the Vestry, and their respective salaries will be found on page 156. STANDING ORDERS. Operative Resolutions in the nature of Standing Orders have been passed during the year as follows:— 19th April, 1893. That overtime made by the foremen or other servants of the Vestry, be paid for with the wages for the week, in which such overtime is made. (W. 14, p. 78-9.) 17th May, 1893. That a schedule of the materials in stock at the Vestry's Stoneyard, be prepared under the direction of the Vestry Clerk quarterly, and that it be an instruction to the proper officers to furnish the necessary information for this to be done. (W. 14, p. 96.) 17th May, 1893. That it be an instruction to the foreman of sweepers to see to the ballasting and watering of the streets as part of his duty, and that when he ceases work, he hand over such work to the foreman of Orderly boys. (W. 14, p. 96.) 17th May, 1893. That the lamplighter be held responsible for lighting, reducing and extinguishing the light in the metered lamps at the proper hours. (W. 14, p. 97.) 14th June, 1893. That each Provisional Valuation List be laid before the Valuation Committee after objections thereto have been disposed of by the Assessment Committee. (Val. 1, p. 41.) 28th June, 1893. That it be an instruction to the Surveyor to arrange for the emptying of street gullies before 8 o'clock in the morning. (W. 14, p. 124.) 25 28th September, 1893. That it be an instruction to the Surveyor to send to the Director-General of Ordnance Survey, early notification of the formation of new highways and roads, and of important alterations in existing highways and roads. (V. 19, p. 492.) 29th November, 1893. That a visiting Committee of three members be appointed each month to inspect the men's Conveniences and Lavatories at Piccadilly Circus from time to time, and to report thereon as occasion requires. (W, 14. p. 211.) 7th December, 1893. That the Surveyor be authorised to sanction the laying of services from mains passing the premises to be supplied, if no distributing box is required. (V. 20. p. 29.) 18th January, 1894. That electric lighting and other Companies having authority to break up the streets, be prohibited from breaking up streets or carrying on other noisy operations in the streets, between the hours of midnight and 5 a.m., except in cases of emergency, the emergency to be established to the satisfaction of the Vestry Clerk or Surveyor. Mr. Daniel Godden, 109, Jermyn Street. Mr. Deasley Andrews, 9, Warwick Street. Mr. Frederick Kyte, 2, St. James's Place. 27 PUBLIC BATHS AND WASHHOUSES. The Vestry avail themselves of the opportunity afforded by the completion and opening of the New Swimming Bath in the Autumn of last year, to present to the parishioners a few particulars relating to the Public Baths and Washhouses of the Parish. The Vestry of St. James adopted the Act to encourage the Establishment of Public Baths and Washhouses within four months of its having received the Royal Assent. On the 26 th August, 1846, the Royal Assent was given to the Act in question, and on the 10th December in the same year the Vestry decided to establish Public Baths and Washhouses in the Parish. Consequently St. James's was one of the first Local Authorities to give the "Ratepapcrs the advantages afforded by the Legislature. Seven Commissioners having been appointed to carry the Act into execution some delay occurred in the selection of a suitable site, in consequence of the difficulty of obtaining land owing to the whole of the parish being built upon. Ultimately, with the approval of the Vestry, Public Baths and Washhouses were erected on the site of 16, Marshall Street, the freehold of which belonged to the Parish, and over a portion of the Workhouse Stoneyard adjoining. The building was opened to the public in 1852 and proved itself an immediate success. In the course of a few years to meet the increased demand for improved accommodation for bathing, especially for women, the Commissioners decided to extend the building, and in 1860 they obtained the necessary consents to appropriate a further portion of the Parish Property in Marshall Street, (Nos. 17 aud 18). The increased accommodation provided by this extension was 28 generally appreciated and the number of bathers and washers continued to increase until the maximum was reached in 1865, when 160,480 tickets were issued to bathers and 70,057 to washers, or a total of 230,537 tickets in one year. In 1890 the Commissioners came to the conclusion that to meet the requirements of the district it was necessary to provide an additional Swimming Bath of modern design, and for this purpose they proposed to utilize, subject to the consent of the Vestry and the Local Government Board, the two houses No. 14 and 15, Marshall Street, also belonging to the Vestry. The consent of the Vestry was given to the proposal, and the Local Government Board held the usual Public Inquiry into the circumstances. Although previous notice of the Inquiry had been widely given only three Ratepayers attended to object. After hearing all the evidence tendered the Inspector remarked that he had held many similiar inquiries but did not call to mind one in which it had been so clearly shown that a bath would impose so small a burden, if any, upon the Ratepayers. The Local Government Board subsequently gave their consent and the Commissioners erected the present handsome Swimming Bath. In a Report presented to the Vestry in January the Commissioners state that after long continued delay the new bath was opened on the 31st July last, and although more than half the Swimming season had then expired the number of bathers who made use of the bath during the remaining few weeks seemed to show that it supplied a want in the neighbourhood, and encouraged the Commissioners to hope for a much better result this year when the bath will be opened lor the whole season. 29 The cost of erecting the original building in 1851, and furnishing and extending in 1861, was about £21,000, which sum was borrowed on the security of the Poor Rate. The last instalment of the loan in respect of this amount was paid in 1891. The cost incurred in the erection and fitting of the new Swimming Bath amounts to £5,849 13s. 8d., after deducting the amount contributed by the Vestry for the construction of the storage accommodation which has been provided under the Baths for the extension of the Vestry's Stoneyard. To meet this expenditure it has been necessary for the Commissioners to borrow a sum of £3,000 from the London County Council and obtain a grant of £1,576 13s. from the Poor Rate. The balance of loan now outstanding amounts to £2,400 which is being reduced at the rate of £300 a year. The total payments from the Poor Rate since the adoption of the Act in 1846 to this Lady Day amount to £36,548 3s. 1d. The Commissioners have, however, applied their surplus receipts, amounting to £9,350, in aid of the Poor Rate making a net charge of £27,198 3s. 1d. on the rates. It will thus be seen that for the sum of £27,198 3s. 1d., the Ratepayers have acquired a freehold building which contains, in addition to the necessary offices, store rooms, boiler house, apartments for superintendent, &c., the following accommodation:— Two Swimming Baths (open from April to October), 1st Class, water surface 60 ft. by 22 ft., Charge, 30 including use of costume, 6d. This bath is devoted to the use of ladies on the whole of Wednesday in each week. Second Class, Charge (Week-days), 2d.; Sunday Mornings, 3d. Private Baths (open throughout the year), 3G First Class (23 for men and 13 for women), Charge, Warm, Bath, 6d., Cold 3d., including use of two towels, 54 Second Class (41 for men and 13 for women), Charge, Warm Bath 2d., Cold 1d., including use of one towel. Laundry (open throughout the year). 84 separate Washing and Drying Compartments, Mechanical Wringers, Ironing Room and Mangling Room. Inclusive Charge 2d. per hour. It appears from the last Annual Report of the Commissioners that the number of Batheis (123,533) for the year 1893 was 14,771 in excess of the number for the previous year. This large increase in the number of bathers is very satisfactory to note, the more so as the new bath is not wholly accountable for the increase, the number of bathers frequenting the new bath being 5,193 The Laundry, however, again shows a falling off, and the Commissioners attribute this to the continued diminution in the residental population of the Parish and the provision of Laundries in many new blocks of dwellings for the working classes. Two Commissioners (Mr. W. Jenkins and Mr. Peyton) retired by effluxion of time in January, and were re-elected for the usual term of office, 31 A list of the Commissioners is given on page 11, and a statement of their receipts and expenditure for the year 1893, and the number of bathers and washers on pages 169-70. The only Charity which is administered by the Vestry is that known as Le Quainter's, which arose from a bequest in 1782 by Mr. Peter Le Quainter, formerly a resident in Piccadilly. He directed that the income should be "equally distributed at Christmas amongst twenty poor persons who are or have been Housekeepers in the Parish, and such as the Rector and Churchwardens and the other gentlemen for the time being who shall compose the Vestry of the said Parish of St. James, shall deem to be proper objects, and the most deserving to partake of the same." c 34 As intimated in the last Annnal Report, the Vestry requested the Charity Commissioners to receive a deputation of five members for the purpose of discussing with them the question of investing the funds of this Charity, which at that time consisted of £9,9G9 2s. 9d., 2¾ per cent. Consolidated Annuities, in the purchase of freehold ground rents or some other security bearing a higher rate of interest than Consols, and the appointment of new trustees of the fund, the Rector being the sole survivor. As a result of this application to the Charity Commissioners the Vestry Clerk had an interview with one of the Official Trustees of Charitable Funds on the subject, who informed him that the Commissioners would not give any general authority for the purchase of ground rents with charity funds, but that they would consider on its merits any application for the purchase of any specific ground rents. Having regard to the possibility of early legislation rendering ground rents liable to local rates, the Commissioners consider that ground rents should be purchased at such a sum as would yield 4 per cent. interest on the outlay. The ground rents must, moreover, be well secured and favourably reported on by a Surveyor or Valuer appointed by the Commissioners. The expense of obtaining professional advice by the Vestry and by the Commissioners, and the legal expense attending the purchase and Stamp Duty would represent a rather large sum to be charged against the capital sum which the sale of Consols would realize. The Official Trustee suggested for consideration the investment of the fund in India 3 per cents., or some other stock in which trustees are authorised to invest by the Trust Investment Act, 1889. The Vestry were advised that the transfer of stock could be effected immediately and without appreciable cost to the charity ; that an investment in 35 India 3 per cents would yield a higher rate of interest than any other stock referred to in the Act mentioned; and that such stock would probably have an upward tendency in the market when the interest on Consols is reduced to 2½ per cent. nine years hence. r The Vestry accordingly took steps to transfer the Consols into India 3 per cents., and at the same time to transfer the stock into the name of the Official Trustees of Charitable Funds. These alterations were carried out and the sum of £9,807 2s. 9d., the proceeds of the sale of the stock belonging to the Bounty, was invested in the purchase of £9,918 13s. 5d. India 3 per cent. stock in which it now stands. It should be stated that the Official Trustees of Charitable Funds are bare trustees without any power over the disposal of the income. In January the Vestry appointed a Special Committee to enquire into the administration of this Charity and to consider as to investing the funds to greater advantage. The Vestry received an invitation from the Vestry of St. Anne, Limehouse, in January last, to appoint t wo Delegates to attend a Conference proposed to be held at the Town Hall, Limehouse, with a view to determining upon some 41 united action to be taken with regard to the continual increase of rates in the Metropolis, and to the formation of a Metropolitan (Non-Political) Ratepayer's Protection Asso ciation. The Vestry, however, informed the Limehouse Vestry that they were not prepared to take part in the proposed Conference. ASSESSMENT OF PROPERTY. The Assessment of the undertaking of the St. James's and Pall Mall Electric Light Company has received consideration at the hands of the Vestry as Overseers during the year, and gave rise to some amount of argument between the Vestry and the Company. It will doubtless interest the parishioners to know the circumstances of the case. When the last general valuation of the Parish was made in 1890, the Company had not then earned any profit from the supply of current, and the Valuation Committee of the Vestry at that time entered the mains of the Company in the Valuation list at an assessment of £100 per mile run, it being understood that the assessment was not to be disturbed until the undertaking had developed sufficiently to justify a re-valuation. Since that time the Company have had continuous and increasing success, so much so that in 1892 they made sufficient profit to pay a dividend of per cent. on their ordinary shares, full interest on their preference capital, and a handsome dividend on the founders' shares, and to carry to depreciation and redemption funds undivided profit sufficient to have paid nearly 10 per cent. more on the ordinary shares. This development of the undertaking, combined with the completion of the Company's new premises in Carnaby 42 Street, necessitated a review of the Assessment and the Valuation Committee in April, 1893, through the Vestry Clerk, placed themselves in communication with the Secretary and Manager of the Company with a view to the mains being re-assessed at a proper amount, and it was suggested that the Company and the Vestry should mutually agree to an assessment., to remain in force until the next re-valuation, to which the Secretary of the Company was understood to have assented. After waiting for some considerable time for figures relating to the undertaking, which the Company had promised to give, but had not done so, the Valuation Committee increased the rateable value of the mains from £250 to £6,480. Against this assessment the Company appealed and claimed to have the rateable value of the mains fixed at £631. The Assessment Committee of the Westminster Union, having-regard to the importance of the case, employed a professional valuer to value the undertaking, which he did as a whole at £9,500, or £1,145 less than the total value fixed by the Overseers. On the hearing of the appeal the Company's Solicitor, without the slightest previous intimation, raised a technical objection that the Committee had only power to increase the assessment by the additional value in the current year as compared with the previous year, and that they had no right to go back to the quinquennial period. The Assessment Committee seemed to think that there was something in the objection referred to, but that the objection was one which should not have been taken, for they disregarded the Company's figures and compromised the assessment of the undertaking as a whole at £7,000 rateable value. Feeling that the Company had not met the Vestry n quite a proper spirit, the Vestry Clerk addressed a communication to the Secretary of the Company on the 43 subject, and subsequently Mr. G. Balfour, M.P., and the Company's Solicitor called upon the Vestry Clerk to explain matters and suggested a compromise. Their explanation amounted to a statement that the Directors were not aware of the arrangement made with the previous manager of the Company in 1890, and they suggested as a compromise that the £7,000 should be adopted as a rateable value without appeal on either side. Having regard to the cost which an appeal to the Sessions and possibly to the House of Lords would involve, and to the small result which it would effect if the Vestry succeeded, as rates on the increased assessment would only be paid to the time of the next quinquennial valuation, the Vestry did not deem it desirable to appeal against the decision of the Assessment Committee. The Vestry, however, informed the Company that they greatly regretted the course which the Company had adopted with regard to the re-assessment of their undertaking, but that, as the difference in amount would work itself out ou the next Quinquennial Valuation List, the Vestry did not propose to appeal, although the only settlement which they could regard as entirely satisfactory would be the assessment of the undertaking at its proper value. It was eventually agreed that the undertaking of the Company should be re-assessed as soon as the accounts for the year 1893 were completed. As mentioned in the last Aunual Report, the Vestry, upon the invitation of the London County Council, deputed Mr. Winnett, the Chairman of the Valuation Committee, and the Vestry Clerk, to represent them at the Conference convened by the Council with a view to securing uniformity of assessment in London. The meetings of the Conference extended over the whole year, the first meeting being held on March 13th, 1893, and the final meeting on March 12th, 44 1894. The resolutions passed by the Conference with a view to promoting uniformity in assessments, set forth the methods to be adopted in valuing different descriptions of properties for the purposes of assessment, and, if followed by the various Eating Authorities in the metropolis, will doubtless tend, to "a large extent, to bring about an equality of assessment throughout London. The Valuation (Metropolis) Amendment Bill, promoted by the County Council last year, also came under the consideration of the Conference as well as the Vestry. The Bill contained some very important alterations in assessment procedure, many of which were considered most objectionable and were strongly opposed by the Members of the Conference, tbe late Vestry Clerk of St. James's taking a prominent part in the opposition to tbe measure. The Bill, for instance, proposed to enable the London County Council to create a Statutory Committee for supervising the assessment of property in the Metropolis, and it was proposed to give the Committee power to appoint officers, incur heavy expenses, and in other respects, to a large extent, act independently of the Council. Clause 19 of the Bill proposed to make it compulsory upon Assessment Committees to appoint expert assistants, subject to the approval of the County Valuation Committee. If, as appeared to be contemplated by the Bill, these assistants were to be permanently appointed, the result would be, not only to largely increase the cost of the valuations of London, without, as the Vestry believed, any corresponding advantage but by limiting their experience, largely dimmish as time goes on, the value attaching to tbe opinion of tbe experts. The most objectionable provision in the Bill, however, was that winch would enable the County Valnation Committee 45 to alter Valuation Lists of Parishes by means of a fiat, thus reversing the accepted form of procedure, and throwing upon Parishes the onus of resisting an order of the County Valuation Committee, instead of requiring the Committee to establish their case, as any other appellant would have to do. The Vestry, while not averse to a well considered amendment of the Valuation laws, were of opinion that the Bill prepared by the advisers of the London County Council was retrogressive in principle, unnecessarily costly in execution, and calculated to work considerable inequality and injustice. They accordingly addressed a communication to the Local Government Board urging the Board not to permit the Bill to proceed further in the House of Commons. Representations on the subject were also made by the Vestry to the London County Council and to the Hon. W. F. D. Smith, M.P. The main features of the Bill were almost unanimously condemned by the Conference before mentioned, and it was ultimately withdrawn by the Council. An amended Bill to meet the resolutions arrived at by the Conference has been introduced on behalf of the Council this Session, but it did not come before the Vestry until after the close of the year to which this Report relates. The Bill is now awaiting its second reading. VESTRY PROPERTY. Vestry Hall.—The Vestry Hall and offices were cleaned as usual during the summer recess, at a cost of £15. The Vestry resolved to provide additional lavatory accommodation for the members by erecting a new lavatory in the rear of the building, in accordance with plans prepared by the Vestry's surveyor, and accepted the tender of Messrs. W. Scrivener & Co., to carrv out the work for the sum of £368. 40 The proposed alterations had not been carried out at the close of the year to which this report relates. Disinfector.—The disinfector has been used for disinfecting bedding, clothing, etc., for parishioneis on 72 occasions compared with 71 in 1892-93 and 57 in 1891-92. Certain repairs to the Disinfector were carried out during the year, at a cost of £10. For the purpose of carrying home clothing after disinfection, the Vestry purchased a truck suitable for the purpose at a cost of £18. Horses.—One of the Vestry's horses (Tommy), bought by the Vestry some 20 years ago, having been certified by the veterinary surgeon to be unfit for work by reason of advanced age, orders were given for the horse to be slaughtered, and for another horse to be purchased at a cost not exceeding £80. Stone yard.—In order to facilitate the lowering and lifting of goods to and from the new stores in the basement under the Baths, a crab and lift were obtained from Mr. J. Stannah, of 20, Southwark Bridge Road, at a cost of £38 exclusive of builder's work. A new stoneyard clerk's office has been erected on the north side of the entrance to the stoneyard, at a cost of £215. The erection of the office in this position necessitated the utilisation of the alternative staircase to the laundry of the Public Baths and Washhouses, to which the Baths' Commissioners gave their consent on condition that the Vestry, at their own expense, entered into an agreement to pay the Commissioners one shilling a year by way of acknowledgment of ownership, and to maintain and repair the superstructure in the event of any subsidence resulting 47 directly or indirectly from the contemplated works. These conditions were assented to by the Vestry. In October last the Vestry approved a plan prepared by their surveyor for asphalting the stoneyard and rearranging the stables. This work involved the removal of the stables to the west side of the yard, and paving the same with blue Staffordshire bricks; the formation of three pits on the east side of the yard, sunk two feet deep, for the storage of ballast, shell, and salt; paving the same with old York ; and the asphalting of the whole of the remainder of the yard on a surface of concrete 12 in. thick, at a total cost of £630. These works were approaching completion at Lady Day, 1894. Mortuary.—The bodies of 27 persons have been received into the mortuary during the year, as compared with 41 during the previous twelve months. The new mortuary and post-mortem room referred to in the last annual report, have been completed and taken into use during the year. A resolution was passed by the Vestry in December last, thanking the Vestry of St. Martinin-the-Fields for their courteous assistance in allowing the use of their mortuary during the rebuilding of that belonging to St. James's. The mortuary-keeper, who also has charge of the disinfector and stoneyard at night, resides at No. 6 Dufours Place, adjoining the stoneyard. The byelaws made by the Vestry with respect to the mortuary are printed on page 68. Medical men, the clergy, district visitors, and others who are specially brought into contact with the poor, are invited to assist the Vestry in preventing the spread of disease which may arise from the retention of a corpse in a room occupied perhaps by a number of people in a thickly. 48 populated neighbourhood, by making known, as occasion requires, the provision made for the reception of bodies in a decent manner, and with all possible deference to the natural feelings of the bereaved relatives. The house adjacent to the mortuary and stoneyard, and known as No. 6, Dufours Place, the lease of which, as intimated in the last annual report, the Vestry had agreed to take, has been appropriated as a residence for the caretaker of the yard and mortuary, and for accommodation for persons temporarily displaced for the disinfection of their homes. A waiting-room for relatives attending the funerals of persons taken into the mortuary is also provided in this building. The premises were repaired and altered to meet the requirements of the Vestry at a cost of £255, and have been found suitable and convenient for the purposes named. As the main object of providing a mortuary and disinfecting apparatus is to protect the parishioners at large against the spread of infectious disease, either may be used without charge. Information as to the mode of proceeding in such a case may be freely obtained at the Vestry Hall. OTHER PARISH PROPERTY. Eleven freehold houses on the east side of Marshall Street were purchased in the year 1819, for parochial purposes. Two of the houses are now absorbed in the Workhouse premises, and the site of five others has been utilised for the erection of the Public Baths and Washhouses. The remaining four houses are let on repairing agreements. The rent 49 received for these four houses, together with the sum receivable from the Westminster Union in respect of that portion of the Workhouse premises belonging to the Parish of St. James, is applied in aid of the Poor Rate. The Guardians of the Westminster Union having under their consideration the question of re-building No. 19, Marshall Street, addressed a communication to the Vestry in April, 1893, suggesting that if the Vestry contemplated dealing with the adjoining property, they would be pleased to confer with the Vestry as to the desirability of carrying out the re-building as a whole. The Vestry accordingly appointed five members to confer with the Guardians on the subject. These gentlemen had an interview with the Guardians, when the subject was fully discussed. While it was recognised at this meeting that it would be very desirable to deal with the property as a whole, certain difficulties presented themselves in regard to ownership, &c., and the Vestry consequently deemed it expedient to appoint a small Special Committee to thoroughly consider the whole question and report as early as practicable. This Committee subsequently presented a Report to the Vestry, which is here inserted for the information of the parishioners:— Report of Special Committee appointed to consider and report on the property belonging to the Parish in Marshall Street. Vestry Hall, Piccadilly, W. 1st June, 1893. The Committee having elected Mr. Bonthron their Chairman, proceeded, on the reference by the Vestry of the 25th May, to consider the question of the ownership of the property in Marshall Street, belonging to the Parish, and the desirability of dealing with the same in connection with the proposed D 50 re-building of No. 19, Marshall Street, by the Guardians of the Westminster Union, and agreed to the following report In the year 1819 eleven freehold houses on the east side of Marshall Street were purchased for parochial purposes from the Earl of Craven for the sum of £6,132. The purchasemoney was apparently paid from the Poor Hate, and the property became vested in the Churchwardens and Overseers of the Poor, under the provisions of the Act of Parliament, 59 Geo. III., cap. 12., sec. 12; latterly, however, the management of the property has been assumed by the Vestry leaving the Churchwardens and Overseers, in whom the fee is vested, as practically bare trustees of the property. Two of the houses and part of the ground originally attached to the property were devoted to the extension of the Workhouse premises, and on the incorporation of the Westminster Union in the year 1868, became the property of the Union under the Act of Parliament, 30 Vict., cap. 6, sec. 75, subject to compensation being paid to the Parish, under the provisions of an earlier Act of Parliament, 5 and G Will. IV., cap. 69, sec. 3. The amount of this compensation is £1,200 per annum which is applied in aid of the Poor Pate of this Parish. It may be mentioned that the new Workhouse building situate in Poland Street was erected at the cost of the Union, on land purchased by the Union, with the exception of a strip formerly used as a right of way from the back premises into Poland Street. The site of five houses has been utilized for the erection of Public Baths and Wash-houses, and the freehold thereof has become vested in the Commissioners without payment or compensation, pursuant to the Act 9 and 10 Vict., cap. 24, sec. 24. The remaining four houses are let on repairing agreements at the following annual rentals:— No 20 at £42. „ 21 ,, £50. „ 22 ,, £45. „ 23 „ £40 51 The tenancy of No. 20 was last year granted to a new tenant, who expended about £140 in putting the premises in a proper state of repair. The Churchwardens and Overseers cannot grant a term beyond their current year of office, and the Vestry, not being the owners, and indeed, being disqualified by the Statutes of Mortmain from holding property for such a purpose, cannot grant a lease of the houses. Although not trust property in the more limited sense, the houses may be described as being applicable to the Poor Law purposes only and not to the purposes of the Vestry. In the year 1886 it was in contemplation to substantially repair the six houses which were then let on yearly repairing tenancies, but the Churchwardens and Overseers, the Owners, and the Governors and Directors of the Poor, who then managed the property, were confronted with the difficulty that they could neither defray the cost of the repairs from the rates, nor mortgage the property, nor create a tenancy for a sufficient term to justify the tenant expending a large sum of money. Under these circumstances the Local Goverment Board were asked to advise the Parish Officers as to what legal power they had to repair or rebuild the premises, and the following is the Board's reply:— As stated in the Board's letter of 7th April last, it does not appear that the cost of repairing or rebuilding the houses can lawfully be defrayed out of the Poor Rate ; and as the Board understand that the Parish do not want to sell the property, they are of opinion that the best course to adopt would be for the property to be let on lease under section 3 of 5 & 6 William IV., cap. 69, subject to the condition that the Lessees shall rebuild the houses, or put them into a proper state of repair. If the property were so let, and it became necessary, before the expiration of the lease, to acquire any part of the property for the purpose of extending the Workhouse, it would be competent for the Guardians of the Westminster Union with the consent of the Board, to acquire the part required under the provisions of sections 51—54 of 30 & 31 Vic., cap. 6 ; or if it is thought likely that the property may d 2 52 be required for that or any other purpose, power might be reserved in the lease for the lessors to determine the tenancy on certain terms. Sec. 3 of 5 & 6 William IV., cap. 69, referred to in the abovementioned communication from the Local Government Loard, enacts that it shall be lawful for the Guardians of any Parish or Union, and for the Overseers of any Parish not under the management of a Board of Guardians, with the approbation and subject to the rules, orders and regulations of the Local Government Board, to sell, exchange, let, or otherwise dispose of any buildings or other property belonging to any such Parish, provided that no such sale, exchange or letting shall take place except with the consent of a majority of the ratepayers of such Parish, and of the owners of property therein, assembled at a meeting of which public notice has been given. A question may arise whether the Overseers or the Guardians are the proper authority to let the property, but, however the property may be let, there is no doubt that if the Guardians require it for Poor Law purposes, and obtain the consent of the Local Government Board, the property will become transferred to the Guardians on payment of compensation to the persons disturbed, and to the Parish as former owners. No doubt the consent of the Local Government Board could be obtained to the property being appropriated, subject to the contingency above referred to, to the erection of dwellings for the working classes under Section 39 of the Housing of the Working Classes Act, 1890, after the Vestry had ordered the demolition of the property as unsanitary and not merely ruinous buildings under other sections of the same Act It is not clear that the Vestry have any power to erect such dwellings at the expense of the rates. Even if they have, it is difficult to see how the Local Government Board can sanction any part of the property being appropriated by the Vestry for Stoneyard or similar purposes in connection with the erection of dwellings for the working classes under the Act referred to. In other words, the Vestry might be able to obtain the consent of the Local Government Board to their taking a lease of the land under the Act 5 & 6, William IV., cap. 69, for a Stoneyard or for any other purpose for which the Vestry are enabled to hold land 53 or to the letting of the land for the erection of dwellings for the working classes under that Act, or the Housing of the Working Classes Act, 1890; but it is not clear how the two could be combined. Being a corporation the Vestry can only acquire or hold lands for such purposes as they are authorised to do by law. If they exceed their statutory powers in this respect, not only would any expenditure be illegal and liable to be surcharged but the land itself would pass to the Crown. Having regard to the difficulties attending the tenure of the property, the Committee regret to have to report that the Vestry are precluded from taking immediate joint action with the Guardians for the re-building of the property. Your Committee recommend that a copy of the foregoing report be sent to the Guardians of the Westminster Union, with an intimation that if the idea of removing the Workhouse in the Country, to which allusion was made at the last meeting of the Vestry, takes practical shape, it would be well worth consideriug whether the Guardians and the Vestry should not co-operate in applying for a Special Act of Parliament to enable the Vestry to deal with the property of the Parish in a comprehensive manner. JOHN BONTHRON, Chairman. In September the Vestry received a communication from the Guardians enclosing a party wall notice under the Metropolitan Building Act, 1855, relating to the rebuilding of 19, Marshall Street, but up to the close of the year to which this report relates no further steps had been taken in the matter. A further communication was received by the Vestry from the Guardians in October last, intimating that it might be necessary for them to acquire the four houses in Marshall Street belonging to the Parish for the erection of a new laundry, and asking what area the houses occupy 54 and the date when the property could be handed over if wanted. This letter was referred to the Vestry's Sanitary and Parliamentary Bills Committee who requested the Guardians to receive a few members of the Vestry in conference to discuss the question of appropriating the Parish property in Marshall Street for the erection of a new laundry and suggested that the first step to be taken at such Conference be to inspect the present laundry accommodation for the Workhouse. To this communication the Guardians replied that they failed to see that any useful purpose could be served by the suggested Conference. As the Committee had no desire or intention to question or interfere with the discretion of the Guardians in the administration of the Workhouse, they expressed their regret to the Guardians that any misunderstanding should have arisen with regard to their attitude in the matter. The Committee were under the impression that if the property in Marshall Street was appropriated for poor law purposes the compensation payable to the Parish in respect thereof would be considerably less than the value of the property based on ordinary commercial principles. Seeing that St. James's already contributes the greater part of the money required for the common charges of the Union, the Committee thought that admitting the new Laundry is required, some alternative proposals might be suggested and considered at a Conference of the kind referred to, with a view, if possible, to some scheme being adopted which would not entail upon this Parish the undue cost involved in the appropriation of the property in question. SCAVENGING, DUST REMOVAL, &c. Under the system adopted by the Vestry, the roadsweepers are employed and paid by the Vestry, but the 55 collection and removal of house dust, street refuse, &c., are done under contract. The total cost of scavenging and dust removal for the past year, as given in the accounts was £8,100 7s. 2d, compared with £7,885 2s. 1d. for 'the previous year. The following is a statement of the number of loads reported to have been removed from the parish during the Year:— Cart Loads. Wagon Loads. Dust nil. 10,086 Slop nil. 5,503 The cost of Street Watering last year was £1,161 2s. 7d. or £120 18s. 10d. more than in 1892-3. WORKMEN'S SICK FUND. A sick fund, on the principle of a slate club, limited to the Vestry's workmen, has been in operation since the 1st August, 1887. The Vestry contribute the sum of 5s. a week to the funds of the club, in lieu of allowing sick pay to individual workmen. The bulk of the surplus is divided among the members at Christmas in the usual way, but one of the rules requires that a balance of not less than £10 be carried forward at the end of each year to provide for the payment of sick allowances before sufficient money has been received from members' subscriptions to meet necessary outgoings. REMOVAL OF SNOW. In anticipation of the approach of winter, the Vestry sought and obtained permission from the Thames Conservators and the London County Council, to cast clean snow 50 over the parapet of the Victoria Embankment into the river. Arrangements were also made for the hire of additional horses and carts should occasion require. The steps taken for cleaning the streets alter each snowfall during the past winter are mentioned in the Surveyor s Report. CONTRACTS FOR WORKS AND MATERIALS. Particulars of the various contracts entered into or continued during the year are given on pages 163 to 165. STREET LIGHTING. On the 25th March, 1893, there were 830 public lamps in the various thoroughfares of the Parish, and this number was decreased by 2\ during the year. At Lady-day, 1894, there were 786 ordinary street lamps, 6 metered urinal lamps, and 35½ larger lamps attached to refuges, &c., making a total of 827½. The cost of lighting 3 lamps on refuges in the Haymarket is borne equally between this Vestry and the Vestry of St. Martin's-in-the-Fields. This accounts for the ½-lamp just referred to. The ordinary street lamps consume 5ft. of gas per hour, and are lighted, extinguished, and cleaned by the Gas Company, at an inclusive sum of £2 17s. 8d. per lamp per annum. As regards the refuge lamps, payment is made according to the consumption of gas as registered by meter. The total expenditure for street lighting during the past year amounted to £2,722 17s. 2d., as compared with £2,686 4s. 4d. for the previous twelve months. This sum is exclusive of maintenance, repairs, and new lamp-posts, lanterns and fittings, which involved further payments amounting to £523 5s. 7d. 57 PRIVATE LAMPS. The Vestry some years since decided not to permit the erection of Private Lamps except upon the following conditions:— 1. That no part of such Lamps shall be less than 10 feet in height from the public footway. 2. That no such Lamps shall in any case project further than the inside of the kerb bounding the footway. 3. That all such Lamps shall be entirely free from writing or any trade devices, except in such cases as Medical Men, Post Offices, Sweeps, Fire Engines, or other positions where they would be a public guide in cases of emergency. 4. That no such Lamp shall be suspended by ball and socket joint only. 5. That no lamps on posts be agreed to unless they are kept lighted the whole night. 6. That a sketch of the proposed Lamps with their dimensions and of any intended inscription thereon, be submitted with the application to the Vestry for approval. ELECTRIC LIGHTING. The second generating station of the St. James's and Pall Mall Electric Light Company, which at the time of the Vestry's last Annual Report was approaching completion, was opened in the month of May, and the Company are now supptying electricity both from their station in Carnaby Street and that in Mason's Yard. The Vestry's attention having been directed to the accounts of the St. James's and Pall Mall Electric Light Company for the year 1892, as audited by the Official Auditor, the attention of the Board of Trade was called to the sum of £3,869 15s. 0d. written off for depreciation, and 58 to the transfer of the sum of £1,000 from Revenue to Redemption Fund. The Vestry felt that when the time arrives for making a representation to the Board of Trade under the 53rd section of this company's order, with a view to obtaining a reduction in the price charged for the current, any undivided profit, such as that before mentioned, should be regarded as forming part of the company s undertaking to the same extent as the profits actually distributed among the shareholders, and they accordingly brought the matter under the notice of the Board of Trade so that it may receive consideration when the time arrives in 189G to apply for a reduction of price. Complaints having been made by inhabitants of the parish of their rest being disturbed, owing to the breaking up of the streets with chisels and sledgehammers during the night by Electric Light Companies, the Vestry, on being informed that the County Council frequently impose a condition, with their consent, that the work shall be proceeded with continuously night and day, addressed a communication to the London County Council in January last, requesting that such a condition should not be imposed in the future, except in cases of absolute necessity. The Council informed the Vestry, in reply, that the condition requiring Electric Light Companies to carry on work in the streets during the night is imposed only in those cases in which it appears necessary in order to prevent prolonged interference with the traffic, and intimated that the request of this Vestry will be borne in mind in future. ALLEGED NUISANCE FROM ELECTRIC LIGHT STATION, MASON'S YARD. It will be seen from last year's report that several complaints have from time to time been received by the 59 . Vestry of the nuisance caused by offensive smells and dust proceeding from the Electric Light Station in Mason's Yard, and that the Vestry had been in frequent communication with the St. James's and Pall Mall Electric Light Co. on the subject. At the time of issuing last year's report the annoyance had been sensibly diminished, although not altogether abated, and the Directors of the Company pledged themselves to devise a complete remedy as soon as the opening of their station in Carnaby Street left them free to effectually overhaul their furnaces and shaft. During the year, however, the nuisance has been as bad as ever, and continued complaints have been made to the Vestry of the annoyance caused to the inhabitants in the neighbourhood. The Vestry's attention was also called to the turning of scalding water and steam into the Vestry's sewer in such quantities as to constitute an improper use of the sewer, and to cause inconvenience and annoyance to the inhabitants and the sewermen, such water and steam being found to emanate from the Electric Light Company's Station in Mason's Yard. In consequence of these complaints the Vestry have directed proceedings to be taken against the Company, either at the Police Court or in the High Court, as they may be advised, with a view to the abatement of the nuisances in question. STREETS PARTLY SITUATE IN OTHER PARISHES. An order was made by the Metropolitan Board of Works on the 6th March, 1857, placing that portion of Oxford Street which is situate in the Parish of St. James under the jurisdiction of the Vestry of St. Marylebone for all the purposes of the Metropolis Local Management Act. The 60 cost of lighting, paving, cleansing, watering, &c., that portion of the thoroughfare is ascertained annually and paid by the Vestry. By an order of the Metropolitan Board of Works, dated the 10th August, 1866, specified sections of the following thoroughfares are placed under the exclusive management of the Vestries of St. James and St. George, Hanover Square, respectively, throughout the entire width thereof, instead of according to the actual Parish Boundary, viz.:— Regent Street, Piccadilly, Burlington Gardens, St. James' Street, and Park Place. No payment is made by either Vestry to the other under this order, the exchange of area being regarded as an equivalent. An order was made by the Metropolitan Board of Works on the 21st December, 1883, placing so much of the carriageway of Wardour Street as lies south of Meard's Court under the exclusive management of the Vestry for the purposes of cleansing and maintenance, and the remainder of the street under the exclusive management, for the same purposes, of the Strand District Board. An arrangement made some years since with the Vestry of St. Martin-in-the-Fields for the apportionment of Coventry Street as regards the cleansing and paving, in consequence of the boundary line being somewhat irregular, is still in force.
