The following private Bills promoted by the London County Council this Session received consideration at the hands of the Vestry:— London County Council (General Powers.) London County Council (Water Bill.) London County Council (Tower Bridge Southern Approach.) London County Council (Improvements.) London County Council (General Powers.) The General Powers Bill of the London County Council deals with a variety of subjects, such as regulating the closing of streets in London; the use of fire hydrants; the lighting of common staircases in tenement dwellings; byelaws as to the conveyance of explosives over the ferries of the London County Council; enforcement of the Ferry bye-laws; the protection of sewers; the arrangement of polling districts and polls at Vestry elections. By Clause 4 it is provided that no street shall be closed or stopped up by a Vestry or District Board during the execution of any paving, sewering, or other works unless with the previous sanction in writing of the London County Council, and subject to any conditions prescribed by such sanction. The clause also provides that if any street is so closed or stopped up without such sanction, or if any of the conditions imposed by the Council are not complied with, the persons responsible shall be liable to a penalty of not exceeding £20, and to a further penalty of not exceeding £5 per day during which such street shall continue closed either without the sanction of the Council or in contravention of any conditions they may impose. 113 This clause is practically an amendment to Section 84 of the Metropolis Local Management Act, 1862, which makes it lawful for a local authority to close or stop up any street in their district with the previous sanction of the County Council. The Act of 1862, however, contains no provisions for enforcing any conditions laid down by the Council, neither does it enable the Council to prevent the closing or stopping up of streets without their sanction. It will be seen, therefore, that the proposed clause if carried into law will prevent local authorities stopping up streets over which they exercise jurisdiction except with the sanction of the County Council, and on such conditions as the Council may impose. This appears to be an unnecessary interference with the powers and duties of Vestries and District Boards as Highway Authorities, and it is rendered more objectionable by the fact that these bodies are to be penalised if they fail to comply with the provisions of the clause or any of the conditions which may be laid down by the Council. Clause 6 provides that the owner of any building designed for use in flats or tenements, in which any staircase or passage is used in common by occupants of different flats or tenements, and is open at night, shall be bound to light every such staircase or passage, and to keep the same lighted from sunset to sunrise on every night to the satisfaction of the Lighting Authority of the district. The Lighting Authority may, by an order under seal, prescribe the amount of light and the positions of any lights to be provided. The owner is to be liable to a penalty of £5 for every night on which he fails to comply with the provisions of the Section. The clause farther provides that the Lighting Authority may undertake the provision and maintenance of lamps and H 114 fittings, and the lighting and extinguishing of lamps on such erms as may be agreed upon with the owner of the premises. It is proposed by Clause 13 to authorise the Council by their officers to enter any premises for the purpose of ascertaining whether the provisions of the Bill relating to the protection of sewers are being contravened, and any person refusing such entry or obstructing any officer in carrying out his duties is liable to a penalty of £20. Clauses 15 to 20 contain provisions for the alteration and re-arrangement of Polling Districts, and by the 17th Clause it is provided that in dividing Electoral Divisions and Parliamentary Boroughs, or any division thereof, into Polling Districts, the districts shall be arranged in such manner so that every elector resident in any Electoral Division, Borough or Division of a Borough, shall be enabled to poll within a distance not exceeding one mile from his residence. No Polling District, however, need be constituted containing less than 300 such electors having votes at a Parliamentary Election for such borough. By Clause 21 it is provided that on the call of a poll for the election of a Vestryman under the Metropolis Local Management Acts there shall be an interval of not less than five clear days other than Sundays or public holidays, between the day on which the notice of poll is published, and the day of the taking of such poll. The Vestry were of opinion that some of the provisions contained in this Bill were objectionable, particularly those provided for by Clauses 13, 17, and 21, which the Vestry felt to be quite unnecessary. Communications were accordingly addressed to the London County Council, to Lord Wemyss, and to the Hon. W. F. D. Smith, M.P., calling attention to the Vestry's objections to the measure. 115 The Bill has been read a second time and referred to a Select Committee for consideration. London County Council (Water). This Bill, which would empower the London County Council by agreement to purchase or take on lease and hold lands and water rights, has been reported by the examiner as not complying with Standing Orders, London County Council. (Tower Bridge Southern Approach.) This Bill would empower the County Council to make a new approach to the Tower Bridge on the southern side of the Thames. The estimated expenditure on capital account for the purpose of the Bill is £436,000. The property proposed to be acquired is situated in the parishes of St. George-the-Martyr, Southwark, Bermondsey, and St. John, Horsleydown. The Vestry did not deem it necessary to take any action on this Bill. London County Council. (Improvements.) This Bill empowers the London County Council to carry out certain improvements and acquire lands for various purposes. By Clause 4, power would be given to the Council to alter and reconstruct the Bridge known as Highgate Archway and the approaches thereto in the Parishes of Islington and Hornsey, and in connection therewith to widen Hornseylane and Archway-road in the said parishes; and to widen Wood-lane in the parish of Hammersmith, at the southern end where it joins the Uxbridge-road. The Highgate Archway improvement is estimated to cost £28,000, of which the Ecclesiastical Commissioners are to contribute £1,000, and the remainder is to be borne in equal H 2 116 parts by the London County Council, the Middlesex County Council, the Hornsey Local Board, and the Vestry of Islington. In the event of the London Street Tramways Company constructing certain Tramways authorised by the London Street Tramways (Extensions) Act, 1888, they will be required to pay towards the cost of the Improvement the sum of £3,000. On the completion of this improvement the Archway is to be maintained and repaired by the Council as a County Bridge at the joint expense, in equal shares, of the Council and the Middlesex Council. The Wood Lane (Hammersmith) Improvement is estimated to cost £5,000, of which the Vestry of Hammersmith is to contribute one half. Clause 6 would enable the Council to purchase certain lands in various parishes for the purpose of the Metropolitan Fire Brigade, Weights and Measures Offices, and Coroner's Courts and Mortuaries, but as none of the sites in question are situate in this Parish, there is no need to mention them in detail. Clause 43 proposes to empower the Council to purchase and take the garden in Lincoln's Inn Fields as an open space for the use of the public. The garden is at present maintained by Trustees under an Act passed in the eighth year of the reign of King George II., who are empowered to levy rates upon the owners and occupiers of certain houses therein specified to defray the cost of maintenance &c. The garden is presumably to be transferred to and vested in the Council in consideration of the abolition or concession of the said rates authorised to be levied by the Act of George II. 117 London Streets and Buildings Bill. This Bill, introduced by the London County Council to consolidate and amend the enactments relating to streets and buildings in London, proposed to repeal and re-enact by means of a private Bill, the substance of several Acts of Parliament, some of which are technically known as public Acts and others as private or local Acts. The Vestry are of opinion that it is very objectionable to entirely repeal a public and general Act of Parliament by means of a private Act; the subject of the proposed Bill, moreover, is of such importance to so large a community that the general convenience would, they think, be best served by the introduction of the Bill as a public Bill, and, if necessary, referred to a Select Committee instead of to a Committee of the whole House, for the consideration of the details A report by the Vestry's Surveyor on certain points which he considered required amendment in the Bill, which throughout is of a highly technical character, was forwarded to tho London County Council for their consideration. LOCAL GOVERNMENT ACT, 1894. The Bill introduced by the Government last Session for the creation of Parish Councils throughout the country passed into law and received the Royal assent on the 5th March last. The Act, as is generally known, was intended originally to apply to the provinces only, but an amendment was inserted in the Bill when it was under consideration by the House of Commons applying certain of its provisions to the Metropolis. So soon as the nature of this amendment became known the Vestry, through their Parliamentary Bills Committee, 118 addressed communications to the then President of the Local Government Board (Mr. Fowler), the Vestries and District Boards of the Metropolis, and subsequently to Lord Wemyss, and the Hon. W. F. D. Smith, M.P., pointing out that not only would the subject of the amendment be more appropriately dealt with in the promised measure for the establishment of District Councils in London than in the Bill in question, but that legislation at the present time affecting the qualification and mode of election of Vestrymen, would probably lead to a comprehensive dealing with the question of Local Government, and the consolidation of local bodies in London, being indefinitely deferred. The provisions of the Act which affect London relate to the qualification of the electors and of the persons to be elected, and to the mode of conducting the election, and are very far reaching in their effect upon the present London Vestries and District Boards. The application of parts of the Act to London necessitate a number of cross references to various sections, and in addition, several sections of other Acts of Parliament are incorporated, thereby making the actual effect of the Act as regards London somewhat confusing. There are besides, two or three apparent anomalies in the Act, which would probably not have arisen had the London clauses formed the subject of a separate measure, and had mor time been given for their consideration. The following extracts from a Report made to the Vestry by the Vestry Clerk, show how the Act affects the present constitution and election of Vestries. Qualification of Electors. Up to the present time tho electors have been those persons who have been rated for twelve months, and were rated occupiers at the time of the election. In future, according to section 31 and sections 23 (3) and 2 (1), which are applied by the former 119 section, the electors are to be the persons whose names appear either in the local government register of electors or the parliamentary register of electors for the parish. Where a parish is divided into Wards the electors of each Ward are, according to sec. 23 (3) to be such of the parochial electors as are registered in respect of qualifications within the Ward. It appears from section 44 (2) that persons on the parliamentary register of electors for the County in respect of the ownership of property in the parish are to form part of the register of electors, and will, therefore, be entitled to vote at Vestry Elections. The persons entitled to vote, therefore, in future at Vestry elections, provided they are on the register of voters, may be summarised as follows:— a) Ratepayers (whether men or women) who have been in occupation of premises for twelve months to the 15th July prior to the election. (b) Tenement occupiers (men or women) in a dwelling house where the landlord does not reside, who have been in occupation for the period above named. (c) Lodgers (male) who have for the like period occupied lodgings of the clear yearly value, if let unfurnished, of £10 or upwards. (d) All male persons inhabiting a dwelling house or room by virtue of any office, service, or employment provided the house is not occupied by the person under whom such man serves. (e) Male owners of freehold property in the parish, provided they are not also registered as occupiers. With regard to the qualification of married women as electors, it is provided by sec. 43 that "A woman shall not be disqualified by marriage for being on any local government rogister of electors, or for being an elector of any local authority, provided that a husband and wife shall not both bo qualified in respect of the same property." Section 44 contains instructions as to the manner in which the register of parochial electors is to bo prepared. A question here 120 arises as to whether the first election, which is to be held in November next, will be conducted on the register of voters to be prepared during the coming summer, or on the register prepared last year. The register of voters to be prepared during the ensuing months does not come into operation until next year; and unless, therefore, the present registration law is altered before November, the first election in that month will take place on the old register with the result that, to be entitled to vote, electors must have been in occupation for twelve months prior to the 15th July, 1603; while any one who has left or altogether ceased his or her connection with the parish since the 15th July, 1893, will be entitled to vote, provided he or she is on the register. Qualification of Persons to be Elected. Section 23 (2), which is made applicable to members of Vestries and District Boards, and to auditors, by section 31, provides that a person shall not be qualified to be elected or to be a "councillor," unless ho is a parochial elector, or has during the whole of the twelve months preceding the election resided in the district, and that no person shall bo disqualified by sex or marriage for being elected or being a "councillor." The twelve months residential qualification inserted in this section was, I imagine, intended to provide for any persons who, being entitled to be on the register of electors, might have been inadvertently omitted from the list. Reading the words literally, however, several important questions are at once raised. For instance, although as previously mentioned a husband and wife cannot both be qualified as electors in respect of the same property, there does not appear to be anything to prevent a husband and wife as well as a large family of sons and daughters, provided they are of full age, from being elected on the Vestry if they have resided in the parish during the whole of the twelve months preceding the election. In fact, there is now practically no qualification needed for election as an administrator of the affairs connected with the local government of Metropolitan Parishes. The provisions relating to the disqualification of members are set our fully in section 46. A person is disqualified if he is an infant or alien; has received union or parochial relief within 121 12 months before his election, or since his election ; has within five years been convicted of any crime and sentenced to imprisonment with hard labour without the option of a fine, and has not received a free pardon ; been adjudged bankrupt, or made a composition or arrangement with his creditors during the time last stated ; holds any paid office, or is interested or concerned in any bargain or contract entered into with the Vestry. The same section provides that if any person acts when disqualified, or votes when prohibited under this section, he shall for each offence, be liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding £20. Section 51 of the Metropolis Local Management Act of 1855 which provides for a penalty of £50 for acting as a Vestryman when disqualified is repealed. Mode of Conducting the Election. The provisions of the Act relating to the conduct of elections are as before stated to apply to the London Vestries, and such elections are to be conducted according to rules to be framed by the Local Government Board (Sec. 23 (5.) If there is a poll it will have to be taken by ballot. The rules to be framed by the Local Government Board in relation to Elections are by section 48 to provide inter alia:— (a) For every candidate being nominated in writing by two parochial electors as proposer and seconder, and no more. (b) For preventing an elector at an election for a parish divided into parish wards from subscribing a nomination paper or voting for more than one ward. (c) For fixing or enabling the County Council to fix the day of the poll, and the hours during which the poll is to be kept open, so however, that the poll shall always be open between the hours of six and eight in the evening. (d) For the polls at elections held at the same date and in the same area being taken together, except where this is impracticable. (e) For the appointment of returning officers for the elections. The Elections (Hours of Poll) Act, 1885, which directs that the poll shall commence at 8 a.m., and close at 8 p.m., is applied to Vestry elections by Sec. 31 (1). 122 It is presumed that under Section 48, the provisions of the Ballot Act, 1872, and the Municipal Elections (Corrupt and Illegal Practices) Act, 1884, and Sections 74 and 75 and Part IV. of the Municipal Corporations Act, 1882, as amended by the last-mentioned Act (including the penal provisions of those Acts) are to apply, subject to certain alterations to be made by the rules, to be issued by the Local Government Board. By Section 48(4) the provisions of the Municipal Corporations Act, 1882, and the enactments amending the same, with respect to the expenses of elections, and to the acceptance of office resignation, re-eligibility of holders of office, and the filling of casual vacancies, are, subject to certain adaptations to be made by the said rules, to apply to elections of members of Vestries under the Metropolis Management Acts. Should any difficulty arise with respect to the holding of the first election, or should an election be defective or otherwise, or should any default occur in the election of Vestrymen or Auditors, the County Council are empowered (Sec. 48 (5) and Sec. 80 (1) to order a new election, or do anything which appears to them expedient for properly constituting the local authority. The expenses of any election are to be regulated by the County Council, and are not to exceed the scale fixed by the Council, and if at the beginning of one month before the first election the County Council have not framed a scale, the Local Government Board are empowered to frame such scale, which shall not be alterable until after the first election. I have not deemed it necessary to detail the provisions of the Ballot Act, 1872, the Municipal Elections (Corrupt and Illegal Practices) Act, 1884, and the Municipal Corporations Act, 1882, which are applied to Vestry elections, as it is not known to what extent these may be varied or modified by the rules to be issued by the Local Government Board. Many of these provisions are very important, dealing, as they do, with the expenses of cand dates, the acceptance of office, resignation, casual vacancies, and other matters in connection with the election. The first election under the Act is, according to section 84, to take place on the 8th day of November next, or such later date 123 or dates in the present year as may be fixed by the Local Government Board. The persons elected are to come into office on the second Thursday next after their election, or such other day not more than seven days earlier or later as may be fixed by or in pursuance of the rules to be made by the Local Government Board. By Section 79 the duty is cast upon the Vestry of taking the necessary measures for the conduct of the first election, including the appointment of the returning officer. Under this section persons who are members of the Vestry at the passing of the Act (5 March) or are auditors are to continue in office until the day on which the members and auditors elected under the new Act come into office, notwithstanding any want of qualification, as if the term of office for which they were elected expired on that day. The meaning of the words "notwithstanding any want of qualification" as in this section is not quite clear, and I hesitatate therefore to express any opinion as to their effect. The annual election of Vestrymen and Auditors will, of course not be held as usual in May this year. Section 79 also provides that of the members first elected under the Act, one third shall go out of Office in May, 1896, one third in May, 1897, and the remainder in May, 1898. Sub-section 6 provides that the members who are to retire in 1896 and 1897 shall be determined according to their place on the poll at the election, those that are lowest on the poll retiring first. If there is no poll, or should there be an equality of votes, the order of retirement is to be determined by ballot conducted under the order of the Vestry. These provisions as to retirement apply separately to each ward. Apparently the dates for the annual election of Vestrymen remain unaltered, except as regards this year, but it should be noted that there will be no annual election in 1895. Miscellaneous Provisions. Section 31 provides that no person shall be ex officio Chairman of the Vestry, and the Rector therefore will, after the first election under the Act, cease to be Chairman by virtue of his office. The Rector and Churchwardens apparently continue to 124 be ex officio members. I use the word apparently as some little doubt appears to exist as to whether section 2 of the Metropolis Local Management Act, 1855, under which these gentlemen act as ex officio members is impliedly repealed. Sub-section (1) of sect. 23 says that "there shall be no ex officio or nominated members of the Urban Sanitary Authority." The question is does this apply to London Vestries ? If it does, then section 2 of Metropolis Local Management Act, 1855, would be repealed as being inconsistent with it. The evident intention of the Government was, I think, that the Rector and Churchwardens should remain ex officio members in London, and as no mention is made of Churchwardens in the recently issued circular of the Local Government Board, I think it may be taken for granted that both the Rector and Churchwardens will remain as heretofore ex officio members of the Vestry. The Vestry, at their first meeting after the annual election, must elect a Chairman for the year, and, according to section 22, such Chairman, unless a woman or personally disqualified, will be by virtue of his office a justice of the peace for the County of London, but, before acting as such, he is to take the oaths required by law to be taken by a justice of the peace other than the oath respecting the qualification by estate. The auditors who, as before stated, are to remain in office in the same manner as Vestrymen until new auditors are appointed in November, will, in future, be elected under the same qualifications as those for Vestrymen, and will be subject to the same disqualifications (secs. 79, 31 and 46). With regard to the effect the Act will have upon the powers and duties of the Vestry, I would point out that section 33, which is made directly applicable to London, provides that the Local Government Board may, on the application of the Vestry, or of any representative body within the district, make an order conferring on the Vestry or some other representative body within the district the appointment of overseers and assistant overseers, the revocation of appointment of assistant overseers, any powers, duties or liabilities of overseers, and any powers, duties or liabilities of a Parish Council. Whether there are any powers or duties which the Vestry might with advantage seek to have placed upon 125 them under this Section I am not at the present moment prepared to say, as the question is a very intricate one, and requires very careful consideration. Certain provisions of various Acts of Parliament as set out in the second schedule to the Act are repealed by Section 89, as also is so much of any Act which is inconsistent with the Act under review. METROPOLITAN STREETS ACT. The Vestry received a communication in April, 1893, from the Commissioner of Police, forwarding a notice stating that an order had been submitted for the approval of the Secretary of State, directing that certain streets be deemed to be within the special limits of the 10th section of the above-mentioned Act. The effect of this order will be to prohibit in the streets specified therein the loading and unloading of coal, etc., between 10 a.m. and 6 p.m., and to give additional powers to the police to regulate the traffic. The streets situate wholly or partly in this parish, mentioned in the notice, are Coventry Street, Piccadilly, Tichborne Street, New Bond Street, Jermyn Street, Shaftesbury Avenue, Pall Mall, Oxford Street, and Regent Street. POSTS IN VIGO STREET. The Bill promoted by the London County Council which had for its object the removal of certain obstructions in public thoroughfares, including the posts in Vigo Street, which at the date of the Vestry's last Annual Report was awaiting the third reading in the House of Commons, passed into law during the year, and the posts in Vigo Street were removed by the London County Council on 120 the 11th November, the site of the obstruction for the future to form part of the street, and to be maintained by the Vestry. In connection with the removal of this obstruction the Vestry widened the carriageway of Vigo Street, so as to be available for a double line of vehicular traffic throughout; paved the western end of the street with asphalte, and relaid the footway paving to the altered line, at a total cost of £300. OVERHEAD WIRES. In accordance with the Bye-Laws made by the London County Council under the London Overhead Wires Act, 1891 (referred to in the last Annual Report of the Vestry), the Vestry in August last called the attention of the several Companies owning overhead wires in the Parish to the duty cast upon them of furnishing the Vestry as the Local Authority with particulars of all their overhead wires and of the penalty which they wero incurring by withholding the particulars so long after the date specified in the Byelaws. In response to this application the Vestry received particulars from most of the Companies owning wires, but considerable difficulty existed in getting the required particulars from the Companies in question in consequence of the large number of overhead wires and attachments which for some time past have been carried through the Parish. As required by the Bye-laws before mentioned the Vestry have approved the samples of insulators, attachments to buildings, &c., submitted by the National Telephone Company and the District Messengers' Service and News Company. 127 PARISH CHURCH CLOCK. The attention of the Vestry having been called to the necessity of repairing the Parish Church Clock, and believing the clock to be a public convenience even more than a want of the Church the Vestry voted the sum of £20, the estimated cost of the Work. OBSTRUCTIONS. The Vestry's attention was called daring last summer, by. a ratepayer, to the obstruction in Regent Street, between Piccadilly and Jermyn Street, caused by the loading and unloading of carriers' vans. The Vestry, however, after giving the subject careful consideration, came to the conclusion that the only action they could take in the matter was to inform the complainant that the Vestry had already communicated with the Polico as the authority for regulating traffic and traffic obstruction, and the Commissioners of Woods as freeholders of the property, on the subject, and that, while sympathising with him, they regretted that they were not able to afford him any remedy. MARLBOROUGH STREET POLICE COURT. In April last year the attention of the Vestry was called to a report that a suggestion to abolish Marlborough Street Police Court was under the consideration of the Government. The Vestry Clerk at once placed himself in communication with The Hon. W. F. D. Smith, M.P., the Member of Parliament for the Borough of the Strand, and the Home Secretary on the subject. The result was that a question was asked of the Home Secretary by Mr. Smith in the House of Commons as to the correctness of the rumour, when the 123 Home Secretary stated that there was certainly no intention of at present abolishing the Marlborough Street Police Court, and that he was in communication with the Treasury with regard to the appointment of additional magistrates, but that no final decision had been come to. On hearing the reply which had been given by the Home Secretary, the Vestry instructed the Vestry Clerk to write to that gentleman conveying an expression of the Vestry's opinion that the requirements of the district, owing to its peculiar circumstances, necessitate the retention of the Court, and that the continued growth of the population and the tendency to confer upon Police Courts jurisdiction in indictable offences amply justify tho appointment ot one or two additional magistrates for the London Police Courts. PRICE OF GAS. In August last the Vestry received a communication from the Vestry of St. Luke's inviting them to appoint three delegates to a conference to be held at the Vestry Hall, City-road, to take into consideration generally the question of the increased charge for gas made by the Gas Light and Coke Company, when Mr. W. Jenkins, Mr. McDonald, and Mr. Frohlich were appointed to represent the Vestry. The following resolutions were passed by the Conference:— (1) That all gas supplied in the Metropolis to private consumers, should be supplied at a uniform charge per 1,000 feet, with the free use of meters. (2) That a Parliamentary enquiry should be instituted into the present management and working of Gas Companies. (3) That the delegates to this conference wait upon the President of the Board of Trade in support of the foregoing resolutions, and (4) That Vestries and District Boards be requested to support the action of the conference. 129 These resolutions were referred by the Vestry to their Parliamentary Bills Committee, and on the recommendation of that Committee the Vestry decided to support the conclusions arrived at by the Conference. Further letters on the subject were received in March last from the Guardians of the Holborn Union, the Vestry of Stoke Newington, and the Board of Works for the Holborn District, when the Vestry informed these bodies of the resolution previously arrived at by them on the subject. FIRE INSURANCE. A communication was received by the Vestry in March last from the London County Council asking for certain particulars relating to certain irrecoverable property belonging to the Vestry in this Parish and enquiring whether the Vestry would be willing to co-operate with the Council in a system of mutual fire insurance. The Vestry furnished the Council with the particulars asked for, but saw no reason for disturbing the existing arrangements made by them for insuring their property, and accordingly informed the Council that they were not prepared to co-operate with them in the matter. USE OF FIRE HYDRANTS FOR FLUSHING AND OTHER PURPOSES. At the invitation of the London County Council the Vestry in November last appointed Mr. Bonthron to represent them at a conference between the Fire Brigade Committee of the Council, the Water Companies, and the Local Authorities, with a view to framing clauses for I 130 insertion in a Bill to bo promoted by the Council in the next session of Parliament to authorise the use of Fire Hydrants for flushing and other purposes. At the conference in question, which was held on the 17th November, a general, although not unanimous, opinion was expressed that it would be an advantage for hydrants to be used for the purposes suggested. Several questions as to responsibility, etc., were, however, raised as to which the Council thought it better to ascertain the views of the several local authorities. The Vestry, after giving the subject careful consideration, informed the Council, in reply to their enquiries, that they would prefer to continue to use independent means of obtaining water for flushing and other purposes, rather than incur the unknown liability attaching to the use of hydrants furnished for fire extinction purposes, and suggested that if the Council contemplate applying to Parliament to authorise the use of fire hydrants for further public purposes, the proposed legislation should take the form of enabling the Council, any local authority, and the Water Company concerned, to enter into an agreement authorising the local authority to use any hydrant or hydrants on such terms as may be mutually agreed. PROPOSED ERECTION OF DWELLINGS BY THE LONDON COUNTY COUNCIL. With reference to the question of the erection of Working Class Dwellings in connection with the various improvements carried out by the Council, the Vestry of the Liberty of the Rolls transmitted to this Vestry a copy of a resolution passed by them, protesting against the erection by the 131 Council out of money raised by rates of any buildings for occupation that will not be self-supporting, aud pay an adequate percentage on the outlay, considering the burden on the Ratepayers at the present time heavy enough without embarking on schemes of philanthropy. The Vestry agreed with the views of the Vestry of the Liberty of the Rolls and addressed a communication to the London County Council on the subject to the effect that, while they understood that the Council had already decided not to erect certain buildings for occupation as dwellings except under conditions similar to those mentioned by the Vestry of the Liberty of the Rolls, they were of opinion that for more than one reason it was desirable that those conditions should apply to every future proposal for the erection of dwellings at the cost of the rates. In reply to this communication the Council called the Vestry's attention to a resolution passed by the Council in March 1893, requiring that buildings to be erected by the Council for dwellings shall be designed so as to provide a net return of not less than 3 per cent. PROPOSED BYE-LAWS FOR GOOD RULE AND GOVERNMENT OF LONDON. In March last the Vestry received a communication from the London County Council, forwarding copy of a report containing information relating to general bye-laws which have been adopted in certain Towns and Counties for the good rule and government of the same, and asking the Vestry to favor the Council with suggestions as to subjects on which it seemed to them that bye-laws might usefully be made for London. I 2 132 The Vestry, in reply, informed the Council that in their opinion bye-laws might usefully be made by the Council, applicable to the whole County of London, dealing with the following subjects:— Storage of Gunpowder. Petroleum. The erection of signboards or other projections more than 12 inches from the face of walls. Control of street musicians. CONCLUDING REMARKS. The Vestry have not attempted in the foregoing Report to touch upon mere routine business requiring attention from day to day, but have endeavoured to submit to their fellow parishioners, in as clear and succinct a manner as possible, a statement of the principles which have guided them iu the discharge of their trust, and particulars of the present condition of the Parish. By order, T. HENSMAN MUNSEY, Vestry Clerk. 133 Supplemental Report of Works executed by the Vestry of St. James, Westminster, DURING THE YEAR 1893-4. LICENCES Have been granted for the erection of 81 hoardings and scaffolds for the purposes of re-building, alterations, &c. Licence has also been given in 37 cases to open the roadway to repair water pipes, or for similar purposes. The cost of making good these openings is charged to the persons taking out the Licences. COAL PLATES. During the past twelve months 20 coal plates were cut into the paving. VIGO STREET. The posts across Vigo Street preventing the passage of vehicles from Regent Street to Burlington Gardens having been removed by the London County Council, your Vestry widened the carriage way to admit of a double line of traffic. The roadway was paved with asphalte. 140 LITTLE PULTENEY STREET IMPROVEMENT. In May, the "Round-House" Public House having been pulled down and set back, as arranged with the Crown Authorities some 10 years since, the widening of Little Pulteney street was continued to Wardour Street, and the Improvement which had been previously partly carried out, completed. GIVE AND TAKE LINE. The building line of Nos. 47 to 53 Marshall Street being very irregular, your Vestry took advantage of the rebuilding of the premises to arrange a give and take line with the owner, thereby greatly improving the footway for pedestrian traffic. REFUGE. A Refuge, lighted with an 80 candle power "Lambeth" lamp, has been placed in the centre of Piccadilly, nearly opposite the Burlington Arcade. ROYAL WEDDING. On the occasion of the marriage of their Royal Highnesses Prince George of Wales, K.G. and Princess " May " of Teck, on the 6th of July, the refuges were removed from St. James's Street for the decorations and the street sanded for the Royal Processions. # FOUNTAIN. An ornamental fountain was erected at Piccadilly Circus, by private subscription, in memory of the late Earl Shaftesbury. 141 STONE YARD. In cousequence of the large amount of room added to the Stoneyard by the annexation of the basement under the newSwimming Bath, the Stoneyard generally has been rearranged; the Stables have been pulled ('own and re-erected in a new position; the space allotted to the Disinfecting Apparatus enlarged, new Mortuary Buildings erected, a new Office from which the Yard can bo well overlooked, constructed with the consent of the Baths and Washhouses Commissioners in the spare entrance to the Laundry, and large bins for the storage of ballast, cockle shell, salt, &c., for use in the streets during bad weather, built. The surface of the yard has been asphalted. These alterations have proved to be a great benefit to the Works Department. LIGHTING. The maintenance and painting of the street lanterns and lamp columns, which were formerly done by the Gas Company, are now carried out for the Vestry by coutract. The contractors for the year were Messrs. R. and J. Shiers of 5, King Street. Regent Street,W. New lamps have been fixed in Beak Street (1), Great Windmill Street (1), and Vigo Street (1 with 10ft. burner), the positions of 1 in Regent Street and 1 in Rupert Street altered, the burner of 1 lamp in Vigo Street increased to 10ft., the burners in the remaining lamps in Vigo Street and the whole of the lamps in Sackville Street increased to 8ft., and the burner of 1 lamp in Rupert Street increased to 7ft. per hour consumption. One lamp has been removed from Rupert Street and 2 from Great Windmill Street The refuge lamps are furnished with a "midnight arrangement," and a man is employed by your Vestry to 142 light, extinguish, and clean these lamps and those in the urinals, and also to reduce the light at 12 o'clock at night. The cost of new lamps, alterations, repairs, maintenance, painting, &c., has been £526 1s. 5d. SEWERS. Examinations of outlets of drains have been made in twenty-three cases. The fee for examination is tive shillings. FLUSHING. The small sewers and courts were flushed at intervals during the hot weather as found necessarv. The cost, of water was £226 0s. 1d.; labour, £G2 l1s. l1d.; and repairs to hose, £38 8s. 3d. DISINFECTING. The gullies and market streets were regularly disinfected during the summer months, but in consequence of the excessively dry weather the number of men employed was double those usually engaged at this work. The disinfectants used for all purposes amounted to 1,913 gallons of sanitary fluid, costing £111 l1s, 10d. 144 URINALS. All the Urinals in the Parish are fitted up on the trough system, and flushed automatically. Excluding the Conveniences at Piccadilly Circus, the water has cost £65 19s. 2d. A constant supply of water is laid on to all the Urinals in the Parish. The cost of alterations and repairs have been £51 1s. 3d., and cleansing £74 1s. 8d. The repairs are principally making good wilful damage caused by persons unknown, and repairing pipes, See., burst during the frost. PICCADILLY LAVATORIES. The cost of general repairs to the Lavatories was £127 0s, 7½d.; gas, including that consumed in the large lamps outside, £85 8s. 4d.; water, £82 6s. 6d. The treads of the steps to the men's Lavatories, which had become badly worn in places, owing to the excessive traffic, were replaced with new where necessary. The wood and ironwork, &c., throughout the building were repainted by Messrs. R. & J. Shiers, of 5, King Street, Regent Street, under contract. In the autumn your Vestry, finding the water closet and lavatory accommodation insufficient, determined to enlarge the building by extending it on the north side under the roadway, and they were thus enabled to add 2 water closets, 5 lavatory basins, and 1 urinal on the men's side, and 1 water closet and 3 lavatory basins on the women's side. A water heater is provided in each lavatory, so that warm water can be supplied to those who require it for washing. Besides these additions the drainage was entirely reconstructed and manholes provided, so that all pipes, &c., can be 145 readily got at. The tile floors of old parts were taken up and replaced with mosaic paving, the brickwork re-pointed, the ceiling covered with 1'Incrusta Francaise, and two Blackman's Air Propellors fitted up for the purpose of extracting the foul air. The work was carried out by Messrs. B. Finch & Co., of 82, Belvedere Road, Lambeth, S.E., under contract. The contract price was £1,562. SNOW STORMS. Soow storms occurred on the 3rd, 4th, 5th and 6th January. On the 3rd the depth of snow on the roadways was 1 inch; on the 4th, 2 inches; on the 5th, 4 inches; and on the 6th, 4 inches. On the 3rd and 4th the snow was all removed each day and the streets swept in the ordinary way before nightfall. The snow which fell on the 5th and 6th was removed from the streets, courts and mews, and the Parish entirely cleared by the 9th January, each street, &c., after it had been cleared of snow, being swept daily in the usual way during this time. 2,842 cubic yards of snow were carted away, the majority being shot into the river Thames from the Embankment. 663 days' work was given to the unemployed. The total cost of removal was £446 15s. 9d. MACHINE BROOMS, &c. The machine brooms required refilling with new bass on the average once in six weeks. The cost of refilling the machine brooms, and new hand brooms and brushes for Orderly Boys, and repairs to the machine brooms, amounted to the sum of £80 3s. K 140 WATERING. The street watering throughout the year was carried out by Mr. William Mead, of Paddington, at a schedule of prices. The water is supplied by the Grand Junction Water Works by contract. The cost of team labour, &c., was £707 16s. 10d., and water, £401 l6s. 5d. STAND POSTS. The cost of repairs to stand posts and swan necks, repacking, &c., has amounted to £23 5s. l0d. ORDERLY BOYS. There are fifteen Orderly Boys at work in the main thoroughfares, under the direction of the Foreman. Bins for the reception of the horse droppings are fixed in the streets at suitable places. DUSTING AND SLOPPING. The contract for dusting and slopping was carried out by Mr. William Mead, of Paddington, at a cost of £5,800. I am, Rev. N a REPORT FOR THE YEAR 1893, made to the Vestry of Saint James's, WESTMI1TSTER/, BY JAMES EDMUNDS, M.D., Member of the Royal College of Physicians of London: Member of the Society of Public Analysts; Fellow of the Chemical Society; Ac., &c., &c.; MEDICAL OFFICER OF HEALTH AND PUBLIC ANALYST FOB ST. JAMES'S, WESTMINSTER. COISTTE3STTS. I.— PUBLIC HEALTH. page General Report for the year 1893 197 Appendix of Tables. 1. Causes of Death 205 2. Cases of Zymotic Disease 208 3. Sanitary Inspectors' Work 227 4. Summary of Sanitary Inspectors' Work 230 5. Underground Rooms cleared of Occupants 231 II.— PUBLIC ANALYSIS. 1. Report on Articles Analysed during year 1893 233 197 TO THE CHAIRMAN AND MEMBERS of the VESTRY OF ST. JAMES, WESTMINSTER Mr. Chairman and Gentlemen, I have the honour to submit my Annual Report upon the Public Health of the Parish of St. James's, Westminster, for the year 1893. The figures given by the Census of 1891 showed that the resident population in St. James's then numbered 24,993, the District of the parish of St. James's covering an area of 162 acres. Taking the population at 24,993 for the year 1891, that would be an average of 154 22 persons per acre against 184 per acre in 1881. The Census of 1891 gave the mean density of the population in Registration London as 565 persons per acre. The position of St. James's as the shopping centre for the best retail trade of the west end of London makes the District more and more a city of luxurious shops, hotels, club', and lodging houses. Increasing facilities for travel to the suburbs, and the increasing value of premises in St. James's, necessitate its utilization for business purposes during the day, and its comparative desertion at night. The crowds of persons who buy and sell in Regent Street Bond Street, aud Piccadilly, and in the network of 198 ing streets, and the workers who are auxiliary to the scrvice of its famous shops now live in large part in the suburbs. Its resident population of 25,000 persons is, therefore, an inadequate exponent of the activity of its daily life, of the importance of its retail trade, and of the necessity for active sanitation. An outbreak of small-pox or of cholera, localized in St. James's, would at once so damage the trade of the district as to inflict upon its ratepayers a thousand times the cost which is now incurred by their preventive sanitary service, and by the prompt removal of infectious cases to suburban Hospitals as is now done. During the year 1893 the following numbers of deaths were registered as having occurred in St. James's:— First Quarter 103 Second Quarter 98 Third Quarter 77 Fourth Quarter 101 Deaths in St. James's during the four quarters of the year 1893 379 To these Deaths there have to be added the deaths in outlying institutions among persons reported as belonging to St. James's 136 515 Deduct deaths of persons reported as Non-Parishioners:— Dying in the Union-House 33 Dying in the Throat Hospital 6 Dying elsewhere 6 — 45 Net Mortality of St. James's for the year 1893 470 199 In a population of 24,993, 470 deaths amount to a death-rate of 18 80 for each 1,000 persons living. During the year 1893, 28 bodies were removed into the Mortuary. Twenty-two inquests have been held upon bodies lying in the Mortuary, and 21 post-mortem examinations for judicial purposes have been made in the Examination Room adjoining the Mortuary. The following table gives a summary of the certified causes of death among persons dying in outlying institutions, but reported as having come from the district of St. James's, Westminster:— Abscess 1 Atrophy 1 Brain Disease 16 Bronchitis 9 Broncho-Pneumonia 3 Cancer 7 Convulsions (Puerperal) 1 Cyst (Abdominal) Ruptured 1 Diphtheria 9 Dysentery 1 Enteritis 2 Epilepsy 1 Gout 2 Haemorrhage (Puerperal) 1 Heart Disease 10 Hyper-Pyrexia 1 Intestinal Obstruction 2 Kidney Disease 9 Liver Disease 1 Neuritis 1 Paralysis 1 Phthisis 29 200 Pleurisy 1 Pneumonia 10 Prostatic Disease 1 Pyaemia 1 Scarlet Fever 2 Small Pox 1 Spinal Disease 1 Syncope 1 Typhoid Fever 2 Violent Deaths:— Fall Downstairs 1 Fall from a Van 1 Run over by Cart 1 Fall downstairs (Fractured Ribs) 1 Scalded 1 Run over by Van 1 Hysterectomy (a surgical operation performed at the Women's Hospital, Soho Square) 1 — 7 136 Against, the above deaths, as affecting the true mortality of St. James's, should be set the deaths of strangers who die in hotels and lodging-houses— many of whom have come to London for medical advice and treatment. A very large number of such hotels and lodging-houses exist in St. James's, but the precise number of the deaths among such visitors is not known. Such deaths, occurring in the district and known to be of persons not belonging to St. James's, have been brought into account in the summary at page 198. 201 The following Table shows the periods of life in which the deaths in St. James's have occurred in the last Seven years respectively. Total 119 136 90 102 77 45 75 76 50 89 48 93 51 57 18 38 36 27 29 26 31 26 26 25 23 During the 25 years, 18C9— 1893 inclusive, the deaths from these Zymotics were 1,471, being an average yearly mortality of 58.84. The Zymotic deaths registered in the Parish during the year 1893 were 23. The Table on page 203 shows the Zymotic and some other deaths in each quarter of the year 1893. All deaths not included in this Table are detailed in Table T., pages 204 to 207. 203 Of the notifiable Infectious Diseases, 262 cases came under notice during the year 1803. Of these 262 cases 107 were of Scarlet Fever; 50 were of Small Pox; 47 were of Diphtheria; 32 were of Erysipelas; 20 were of Typhoid; 3 were of Continued Fever; and 3 were of Puerperal Fever. Of the 202 cases, 159 were removed to Extra-Parochial Hospitals, and 5 to the Poor Law Infirmary in Cleveland Street; 08 of the cases were not removed. Details of these 262 cases are appended in Table II, pages 208 to 220. WILLIAM HILL WATSON, Chief Sanitary Inspector. 233 SALE OP FOOD AND DRUGS ACTS. REPORT UPON ARTICLES ANALYSED DURING THE YEAR 1893, MADE TO THE Vestry of St. James's, Westminister, BY JAMES EDMUNDS, M.D., M.R.C.P. Lond., F.C.S., &c., Medical Officer of Health and public Analyst for St. James's, Westminster. Mr. Chairman and Gentlemen, During the year 1893, under the provisions of the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts, 83 samples were examined, all which were procured for examination by the Vestry Officers. In none of these samples was any poisonous ingredient discovered. Among the samples submitted for examination, there have been the following:— Milk 32 Vinegar 24 Butter 12 Coffee 7 Cocoa 4 Arrowroot 3 Wine 1 83 234 Of the Milk samples, 5 were adulterated with water and the vendors prosecuted and fined (see Table); and 5 were found very poor, the vendors of these were warned by letter from the Vestry Clerk. Of the Vinegar samples, 4 contained less than 4 per cent. of real Acetic Acid (C2H402); their vendors were warned that these Vinegars were too weak. No. 57 was certified as containing 22 per cent. of added water; the vendor was prosecuted, but acquitted. The accuracy of the analysis made in St. James's was fully admitted, but the defence turned upon what standard should be taken for vinegar. The magistrate decided that the weakest vinegar might possibly contain only 3 per cent. of Acetic Acid, and the defendant was thereupon acquitted. In vinegar No. 74, free Sulphuric Acid (.1275 per cent.) was found. In my opinion, the addition of Sulphuric Acid to Vinegar is a fraudulent and injurious act, but, owing to the uncertain state of the law, and the fact that the old Vinegar Act allowed for excise purposes one thousandth part by weight of Oil of Vitriol to exist in vinegar, I did not advise a prosecution. The vendor of this vinegar was warned. The question of prosecuting will be reconsidered in the event of free Sulphuric Acid being again found in Vinegar. Upon the Law relating to the Sale of Vinegar containing Sulphuric Acid, the following report was made to the Sanitary Committee by Harry Wilkins, Esquire, Barristerat-Law, Clerk to the Vestry of St. James. "Apart altogether from statute law, a purchaser has a right to obtain the article for which he pays the price. If any article of food, or used in the preparation of food, is sold in such a 235 state, whether arising from adulteration or decomposition, as to be injurious to the health of the purchaser, the vendor subjects himself, not only to a civil action for damages, but also to the liability of an indictment. "Statute law relating to adulteration may be roughly divided into two classes:— "(1.) Restrictions imposed for the purposes of Revenue; and "(2.) Acts passed for the protection of the purchaser from fraud. "Prosecutions under Acts of Parliament falling within the former of these two classes can only be undertaken by officers appointed by the Government, while Acts of the second class are administered by Local Sanitary Authorities, such as the Vestry, and proceedings can be maintained under them by private individuals, independently of the Vestry altogether. It is only with these last-mentioned Acts that the Committee need trouble themselves. "For all practical purposes the law relating to adulteration, so far as concerns Local Authorities, has been codified in the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts of 1875 and 1879, although they are supplemented in the Margarine Act, 1887, and one or two other Acts. Offences under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts may, for the purpose of this report, be classified under three heads:— "(1.) The fraudulent addition of a substance injurious to health; "(2.) The fraudulent abstraction of an ingredient; and “(8.) The sale, even without any allegation of fraud, of an article not of the nature, substance, or quality demanded by the purchaser. "The sale of Vinegar containing Sulphuric Acid might come under cither the first or third of these principal heads; but it is clear that to support a prosecution for an offence of the first class the evidence must be stronger and more direct than in the case of a prosecution under the third head. The 3rd Section of the Sale of Food and Drugs Act, 1875, imposes a penalty, for tho first offence, of £50 upou any person who mixes any article of food with any ingredient or material so 236 as to render the article injurious to health, with intent that the same may be sold in that state; and a similar penalty is imposed on any person selling such article. The 5th Section, however, exempts from the penalty any person who proves that he did not know of the article being so mixed, and that he could not. with reasonable diligence, have obtained that knowledge. It will be seen that, not only must the article have been rendered injurious to health, but also that intent to sell in the mixed state must be proved if the manufacturer is proceeded against, and that the actual vendor can set aside the prosecution by proving absence of knowledge, and that he could not reasonably obtain such knowledge. A prosecution under the 3rd Section should, therefore, not be lightly undertaken. "Turning to the third class of offence, it may be remarked that, if a purchaser asks for vinegar, and receives, without notice from the vendor, vinegar plus sulphuric acid, he no more obtains an article of the nature demanded than a purchaser who asks for milk and receives milk and water, unless, indeed, the presence of sulphuric acid is a necessary or a customary result of the manufacture of vinegar. From the fact that the Vinegar Act (58 Geo. III., cap. 65), which was a Revenue Act and is now repealed, permitted the presence of a small percentage of sulphuric acid, I infer that it was, and perhaps is, customary for makers of vinegar to sharpen the acidity of their article by the addition of sulphuric acid, and that the presence of a small quantity of this acid was not regarded as harmful to the consumer. If the Committee contemplate undertaking a prosecution for the sale of Vinegar containing Sulphuric Acid, the safest course would be to take proceedings under the 6th Section of the Act of 1875—that is, for the sale of an article not of the nature demanded by the purchaser, which would not necessitate proof that the sulphuric acid was added to the vinegar, but would throw upon the vendor the onus of proof hat sulphuric acid is a usual ingredient of commercial vinegar. At the same time, it would be prudent for the Committee to satisfy themselves that sulphuric acid is not a usual ingredient of commercial vinegar before deciding to take any proceedings at all. "HARRY WILKINS, “Vestry Clerk. "20th January, 1894." 237 Of the 12 samples of Butter, 1 was found to contain 90 per cent. of Margarine; the vendor of this butter was prosecuted and fined; the 11 other samples were pure butters. Of the 4 samples of Cocoa, 2 contained respectively 50 per cent. and 40 per cent of potato starch. The first of these samples was labelled “Sold as a Mixture," and was therefore unassailable; the vendor of the second sample was warned. The 2 other samples were genuine. The 3 samples of Arrowroot were genuine. The sample of Claret, labelled “Grand Vin Margaux,” was found to be very acid and to contain some deposit, but no evidence of adulteration was discovered. No money or consideration, other than the stipend paid by the Vestry, has been received by me in connection with these analyses. I have the honour to remain, Mr. Chairman and Gentlemen, Your obedient Servant, JAMES EDMUNDS. 29, Dover Street, Piccadilly. 238 Table of 83 Samples submitted for examination during the year 1893.
